ومما يتعلق بأم الولد حكاية لطيفة ذكرها في المعراج لما أخرج شمس الأئمة من السجن زوج السلطان أمهات الأولاد من خدامه الأحرار فسأل العلماء عن هذه فقالوا: نعم ما فعلت فقال الأئمة له أخطأت لأن تحت كل خادم حرة وهذا تزوج الأمة على الحرة فقال السلطان اعتقهن وأجدد العقد فسأل العلماء فقالوا: نعم ما فعلت. فقال شمس الأئمة له : أخطأت لأن العدة تجب عليهن بعد الإعتاق فكان المعتدة تزویج الغير، فأنسى الله من تعالى العلماء الجواب في هاتين المسألتين ليظهر فضل شمس الأئمة اهـ. ولكن حكاها محب الشحنة فيما كتبه على الهداية على غير هذا لوجه وهو أنه لما خطأه في الثانية أغراه عليه القاضي فحبسه وأن هذا كان سبب حبسه ، أن القاضي حينئذ كان فخر الإسلام البزدوي، وأن طلبته وعلماء عصره لا ينقطعون عنه ولا يتركون الاشتغال عليه فمنعوا عنه كتبه فأملى المبسوط من حفظه . وقيل : كان سبب حبسه أن السلطان أراد أن يأخذ من الرعية مظلمة كبيرة ثم ترك بعضها فمدحه القاضي فأنكر عليه شمس الأئمة فقال : لا يمدح إذا ترك جميعه فكيف بترك بعضه؟ فحبسه . وحكى شمس الأئمة في المبسوط واقعة مناسبة للموطوءة بشبهة دالة على أفضلية الإمام شمس الدين بن العلماء رضي الله تعالى عنه على علماء زمانه هي : رجل زوج ابنيه بنتين وعمل الوليمة وجمع وفيهم أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه لكنه لم يكن حينئذ من المشهورين ففي أثناء الليل سمعوا ولولة النساء فسألوا فأخبروا انهن غلطن فأدخلت زوجة كل أخ على أخيه فسألوا العلماء فأجابوا بأن كل واحد يجتنبها حتى تنقضي عدتها فتعود إلى زوجها فعسر ذلك الجواب فقال الإمام رضي الله عنه : يطلق كل زوجته ويعقد على موطوءته ويدخل عليها للحال لأنه صاحب العدة بعد ما سأل كل واحد من الأخوين عن مراده فقال كل مرادي موطوءتي لا المعقود عليها فرجع العلماء إلى جوابه.
And among things related to umm walad is a delightful story mentioned in al-Mi'raj: When Shams al-A'imma was released from prison, the Sultan married the ummahat al-awlad (mothers of children) to his free servants. He asked the scholars about this, and they said: 'What you did is good.' The imam said to him: 'You erred, because under each servant is a free woman, and this is marrying a slave woman over a free woman.' The Sultan said: 'Free them and renew the contract.' He asked the scholars, and they said: 'What you did is good.' Shams al-A'imma said to him: 'You erred, because the 'iddah becomes obligatory on them after emancipation, so a woman in 'iddah is marrying someone else.' Thus Allah made the scholars forget the answer in these two issues to manifest the virtue of Shams al-A'imma. End. But Mahb al-Shihna narrated it in his commentary on al-Hidayah differently: that when he [Shams al-A'imma] corrected him in the second issue, the judge incited the Sultan against him and imprisoned him, and this was the cause of his imprisonment. The judge at that time was Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. His students and scholars of his time did not cease visiting him and did not leave off studying with him, so they prevented his books from him, and he dictated al-Mabsut from memory. And it was said: the cause of his imprisonment was that the Sultan wanted to take a great injustice from the subjects, then left part of it, so the judge praised him, but Shams al-A'imma objected, saying: 'He should not be praised if he left all of it, then how about leaving part of it?' So he imprisoned him. And Shams al-A'imma narrated in al-Mabsut a story relevant to a woman who is penetrated under a shubha, indicating the superiority of Imam Shams al-Din ibn al-'Ulama' (may Allah be pleased with him) over the scholars of his time: A man married his two sons to two daughters and held a wedding feast, and among the attendees was Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) though he was not then well-known. During the night they heard the wailing of women; they asked and were told that they had mistaken, and each brother's wife was brought to the other brother. They asked the scholars, who answered that each one should avoid her until her 'iddah expires, then she returns to her husband. That answer was difficult. Then the Imam (Abu Hanifa) said: 'Let each husband divorce his wife and contract marriage with the woman he actually penetrated, and enter upon her immediately, because he is the one who owns the 'iddah.' After he asked each of the two brothers about his intent, each said: 'My intent is the woman I penetrated, not the one I contracted with.' So the scholars retracted to his answer.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This biographical passage narrates two stories related to Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani (a major Hanafi jurist) and Abu Hanifa. The first story shows Shams al-A'imma's correct fiqh when other scholars erred regarding marrying ummahat al-awlad (slave concubines who bore children) to free men, pointing out that after emancipation they must observe 'iddah before remarrying. The second story, attributed to Abu Hanifa himself, deals with a wedding mix-up where two brothers accidentally consummated with each other's wives. Other scholars gave a difficult solution requiring extended avoidance and 'iddah, but Abu Hanifa gave a practical solution: each divorces his contracted wife and immediately contracts marriage with the woman he actually slept with, since the 'iddah of consummation (being the real one) belongs to him. The text highlights the superior knowledge of these imams.

Key Terms
شمس الأئمة (Shams al-A'imma): Title of the Hanafi jurist Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi, known for his work al-Mabsut.
أم الولد (umm walad): A slave-concubine who bears her owner's child; upon his death, she becomes free.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or emancipation before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the women were still owned by the Sultan
B) Because the women were in 'iddah
C) Because the servants were not Muslims
D) Because the marriages were not witnessed

Key Takeaway
Emancipation does not waive 'iddah; a freed umm walad must wait before remarrying.

Abu Hanifa and the Wedding Mix-Up
Biographical anecdote with fiqh ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that when a marriage is consummated with the wrong person, the marriage can be corrected by divorce and new marriage, recognizing the 'iddah of the actual consummator.

Core Idea
Consummation creates marriage: if a wedding mix-up occurs, divorce and remarry the actual partner.

This story from the life of Abu Hanifa (before he was widely known) demonstrates his quick and sound legal reasoning. At a double wedding feast, the brides were mistakenly sent to the wrong brothers. The scholars' solution required each brother to avoid his unintended wife until her 'iddah expired, then she would return to the correct husband. Abu Hanifa offered a simpler, more practical solution: each divorces the contracted wife and immediately marries the woman he actually slept with, because the 'iddah belongs to the one who consummated, and each brother's intention was for that woman. This story illustrates the Hanafi emphasis on the actual consummation and intention.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Two brothers married two daughters of a man. At the wedding feast, the brides were mistakenly sent to the wrong brother, and each consummated with the other's contracted wife.
Abu Hanifa was present but not yet famous.
2
Identify the scholars' initial solution
They said each brother should avoid the woman he slept with until her 'iddah from the consummation expires, then she returns to her contracted husband. This is a cautious approach.
This solution involves prolonged separation.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's alternative
He asked each brother: 'Whom did you intend to marry?' Each replied: 'The woman I slept with.' He then ruled: divorce the contracted wife, and marry the consummated one immediately because the 'iddah belongs to the one who consummated, not the contracted husband.
Key principle: the consummation establishes the marriage in terms of 'iddah and intention.
4
Extract the Hanafi ruling
When a man consummates with a woman by mistake, and both acknowledge the error, the marriage can be regularized by divorce of the contracted wife and immediate marriage to the actual partner, as long as the 'iddah of the actual partner is with the man who consummated.
The 'iddah is transferred to the new husband because he is the one who caused it.

ومما يتعلق بأم الولد حكاية لطيفة ذكرها في المعراج لما أخرج شمس الأئمة من السجن زوج السلطان أمهات الأولاد من خدامه الأحرار فسأل العلماء عن هذه فقالوا: نعم ما فعلت فقال الأئمة له أخطأت لأن تحت كل خادم حرة وهذا تزوج الأمة على الحرة فقال السلطان اعتقهن وأجدد العقد فسأل العلماء فقالوا: نعم ما فعلت. فقال شمس الأئمة له : أخطأت لأن العدة تجب عليهن بعد الإعتاق فكان المعتدة تزویج الغير، فأنسى الله من تعالى العلماء الجواب في هاتين المسألتين ليظهر فضل شمس الأئمة اهـ. ولكن حكاها محب الشحنة فيما كتبه على الهداية على غير هذا لوجه وهو أنه لما خطأه في الثانية أغراه عليه القاضي فحبسه وأن هذا كان سبب حبسه ، أن القاضي حينئذ كان فخر الإسلام البزدوي، وأن طلبته وعلماء عصره لا ينقطعون عنه ولا يتركون الاشتغال عليه فمنعوا عنه كتبه فأملى المبسوط من حفظه . وقيل : كان سبب حبسه أن السلطان أراد أن يأخذ من الرعية مظلمة كبيرة ثم ترك بعضها فمدحه القاضي فأنكر عليه شمس الأئمة فقال : لا يمدح إذا ترك جميعه فكيف بترك بعضه؟ فحبسه . وحكى شمس الأئمة في المبسوط واقعة مناسبة للموطوءة بشبهة دالة على أفضلية الإمام شمس الدين بن العلماء رضي الله تعالى عنه على علماء زمانه هي : رجل زوج ابنيه بنتين وعمل الوليمة وجمع وفيهم أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه لكنه لم يكن حينئذ من المشهورين ففي أثناء الليل سمعوا ولولة النساء فسألوا فأخبروا انهن غلطن فأدخلت زوجة كل أخ على أخيه فسألوا العلماء فأجابوا بأن كل واحد يجتنبها حتى تنقضي عدتها فتعود إلى زوجها فعسر ذلك الجواب فقال الإمام رضي الله عنه : يطلق كل زوجته ويعقد على موطوءته ويدخل عليها للحال لأنه صاحب العدة بعد ما سأل كل واحد من الأخوين عن مراده فقال كل مرادي موطوءتي لا المعقود عليها فرجع العلماء إلى جوابه.
And among things related to umm walad is a delightful story mentioned in al-Mi'raj: When Shams al-A'imma was released from prison, the Sultan married the ummahat al-awlad (mothers of children) to his free servants. He asked the scholars about this, and they said: 'What you did is good.' The imam said to him: 'You erred, because under each servant is a free woman, and this is marrying a slave woman over a free woman.' The Sultan said: 'Free them and renew the contract.' He asked the scholars, and they said: 'What you did is good.' Shams al-A'imma said to him: 'You erred, because the 'iddah becomes obligatory on them after emancipation, so a woman in 'iddah is marrying someone else.' Thus Allah made the scholars forget the answer in these two issues to manifest the virtue of Shams al-A'imma. End. But Mahb al-Shihna narrated it in his commentary on al-Hidayah differently: that when he [Shams al-A'imma] corrected him in the second issue, the judge incited the Sultan against him and imprisoned him, and this was the cause of his imprisonment. The judge at that time was Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. His students and scholars of his time did not cease visiting him and did not leave off studying with him, so they prevented his books from him, and he dictated al-Mabsut from memory. And it was said: the cause of his imprisonment was that the Sultan wanted to take a great injustice from the subjects, then left part of it, so the judge praised him, but Shams al-A'imma objected, saying: 'He should not be praised if he left all of it, then how about leaving part of it?' So he imprisoned him. And Shams al-A'imma narrated in al-Mabsut a story relevant to a woman who is penetrated under a shubha, indicating the superiority of Imam Shams al-Din ibn al-'Ulama' (may Allah be pleased with him) over the scholars of his time: A man married his two sons to two daughters and held a wedding feast, and among the attendees was Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) though he was not then well-known. During the night they heard the wailing of women; they asked and were told that they had mistaken, and each brother's wife was brought to the other brother. They asked the scholars, who answered that each one should avoid her until her 'iddah expires, then she returns to her husband. That answer was difficult. Then the Imam (Abu Hanifa) said: 'Let each husband divorce his wife and contract marriage with the woman he actually penetrated, and enter upon her immediately, because he is the one who owns the 'iddah.' After he asked each of the two brothers about his intent, each said: 'My intent is the woman I penetrated, not the one I contracted with.' So the scholars retracted to his answer.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This biographical passage narrates two stories related to Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani (a major Hanafi jurist) and Abu Hanifa. The first story shows Shams al-A'imma's correct fiqh when other scholars erred regarding marrying ummahat al-awlad (slave concubines who bore children) to free men, pointing out that after emancipation they must observe 'iddah before remarrying. The second story, attributed to Abu Hanifa himself, deals with a wedding mix-up where two brothers accidentally consummated with each other's wives. Other scholars gave a difficult solution requiring extended avoidance and 'iddah, but Abu Hanifa gave a practical solution: each divorces his contracted wife and immediately contracts marriage with the woman he actually slept with, since the 'iddah of consummation (being the real one) belongs to him. The text highlights the superior knowledge of these imams.

Key Terms
وليمة (walimah): The wedding feast, a recommended sunnah in marriage.
موطوءة (mawtu'ah): A woman who has been penetrated (in this context, the woman each brother actually slept with).
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or mistake that can affect the legal ruling, often mitigating the penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the key element in Abu Hanifa's solution that made it acceptable?
A) The brothers divorced their wives first
B) The brothers stated their intention to marry the woman they slept with
C) The women consented
D) The original marriage contracts were invalid

Key Takeaway
Consummation with intention to marry creates a valid marriage, allowing a practical solution in mix-up scenarios.

Ruling on Iddah in Fasid Marriage When Husband Denies Intercourse
Ruling on iddah in a fasid marriage when husband denies intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the husband denies intercourse in a fasid marriage and distinguish who has the burden of proof for iddah versus mahr.

Core Idea
Wife's claim imposes iddah; husband's denial spares mahr.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from al-Qunyah regarding a fasid (irregular) marriage. When the husband denies consummation but the wife claims it, the law splits the consequences: iddah is obligatory based on her statement, while mahr is not due based on his denial. Understanding this distinction is key to applying Hanafi fiqh in such scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that the marriage is fasid (irregular), not batil (void). The husband denies intercourse; the wife claims it and says she is not balighah.
Fasid marriage can produce some legal effects if consummated.
2
Extract the two separate rulings
First ruling: The wife must observe iddah. Second ruling: The husband is not liable for mahr. These depend on different claims.
Iddah is obligatory even without proof; mahr requires admission.
3
Understand the rationale
Iddah protects lineage and prevents marriage to another. Mahr is a financial obligation that requires evidence of consummation or promise.
The law balances interests: certainty of lineage vs. protection from false claims.
4
Note the burden of proof
The wife's word is accepted for iddah. The husband's word is accepted for mahr. This is a split in evidentiary weight.
The wife's claim triggers iddah; the husband's denial prevents mahr.
5
Apply to a similar scenario
Consider a fasid marriage where the wife claims intercourse but the husband denies. The judge orders iddah but does not order mahr unless other evidence appears.
This ruling prevents lineage confusion without imposing financial harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : تزوجها نكاحاً فاسداً وأنكر الدخول وهي تزعم أنها غير بالغة وأنه دخل بها لزمتها العدة حتى يحرم نكاحها على غيره .اهـ. فعلى هذا القول قوله في الدخول وعدمه في حق المهر وقولها في وجوب العدة .
And in al-Qunyah: He married her with a fasid (invalid) marriage and denied intercourse, while she claims that she is not of age (balighah) and that he had intercourse with her. The iddah becomes obligatory upon her so that her marriage to another is prohibited. So based on this, his word regarding intercourse or its absence is accepted in the matter of mahr, and her word is accepted regarding the necessity of iddah.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage from al-Qunyah addresses a situation where a man marries a woman in a fasid (irregular) marriage, such as one missing a condition. After the marriage, the husband denies having consummated it, but the wife claims she is not yet balighah (mature) and that he did have intercourse with her. The ruling is that the woman must observe iddah (waiting period) to prevent her from marrying another, because her claim of intercourse is accepted for the purpose of iddah. However, regarding the mahr (dower), the husband's word is accepted: if he denies intercourse, no mahr is due; if he admits, mahr is due. This shows a split: the wife's claim is sufficient to impose iddah (to avoid mixing lineages), but the husband's denial is sufficient to avoid financial obligation. This balances the interests of the parties.

Key Terms
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An irregular marriage that is invalid in essence but may produce some legal effects if consummated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In a fasid marriage, the wife's claim suffices for iddah but not for mahr; the husband's denial prevents mahr.

The Start of 'Iddah in Invalid Marriage and Conditions for Mutaraka
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'iddah timing and conditions for mutaraka

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when 'iddah begins in an invalid marriage and explain the conditions for a valid mutaraka.

Core Idea
In invalid marriage, 'iddah begins only after explicit separation, not from the last intercourse.

In an invalid marriage (nikah fasid), the timing of 'iddah is a point of dispute within the Hanafi school. This passage explains why the majority holds that 'iddah starts after separation or a firm intention to abstain, not from the last intercourse. It also clarifies the essential conditions for mutaraka, including the requirement of explicit words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that Zufar argues 'iddah begins from the last intercourse, while the Hanafi majority says it begins after separation or definite abstention.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
All acts of intercourse in an invalid marriage are treated as one act under a single contract, so the cause is not complete until separation.
This is based on qiyas jali: unification of contract.
3
Apply the condition for 'iddah start
Before mutaraka or determination, 'iddah does not begin because further intercourse is possible.
Mere possibility prevents commencement.
4
Analyze conditions for mutaraka
Mutaraka must be by explicit words (e.g., 'I leave you'), not by absence or denial of marriage. Knowledge by the other party is required according to one opinion.
Absence does not constitute mutaraka.
5
Note practical application
The practical consequence: under Hanafi view, remarriage of the woman is delayed until after separation and completion of 'iddah.
This ensures no overlapping 'iddahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وفي النكاح الفاسد بعد التفريق أو العزم على ترك وطئها) أي مبدأ العدة. وقال زفر: من آخر الوطات لأن الوطء هو السبب الموجب. ولنا أن كل وطء وجد في العقد الفاسد يجري مجرى الوطأة الواحدة لاستناد الكل إلى حكم عقد واحد ولهذا يكتفي في الكل بمهر واحد، فقبل المتاركة أو العزم لا تثبت العدة مع جواز وجود غيره، ولأن التمكن على وجه الشبهة أقيم مقام حقيقة الوطء لخفائه ومساس الحاجة إلى معرفة الحكم في حق غيره. وفي الخلاصة: المتاركة في النكاح الفاسد بعد الدخول لا تكون إلا بالقول كقوله تركتك أو يقوم مقامه كتركتها أو خليت سبيلها، أما عدم المجيء فلا لأن الغيبة لا تكون متاركة لأنه لو عاد تعود ولو أنكر نكاحها لا تكون متاركة. وقدمنا في النكاح الفاسد أنهما لو اختلفا في الدخول فالقول له في المهر فلا يجب المهر وأن المراد بهذه العدة عدة المتاركة فلا عدة عليها بموته إلا الحيض بعد الدخول، وأنه لا حداد ولا نفقة فيها، وإن تزوج أخت امرأته فاسداً تحرم عليه إلى انقضاء عدتها وأن وجوبها فيه إنما هو في القضاء، أما في الديانة لو علمت أنها حاضت بعد آخر وطء ثلاثاً حل لها التزوج من غير تفريق ونحوه وأن الطلاق فيه متاركة وأن إنكار النكاح إن كان بحضرتها فمتاركة وإلا فلا وإن علم غير المتاركة بالمتاركة شرط على قول وصحح، وقيل لا وصحح ورجحنا الثاني، وأن المتاركة لا تختص بالزوج بل تكون من المرأة أيضاً ولذا ذكر مسكين في شرحه من صورها أن تقول له تركتك وقدمنا كثيراً من أحكامه هناك فارجع إليه وبما قررناه علم أن مجرد العزم لا يكفي بل لا بد من الإخبار بما يدل عليه ولذا قال في العناية: العزم أمر باطن لا يطلع عليه وله دليل ظاهر وهو الإخبار به فلو قال كما في الإصلاح أو إظهار عزمه لكان أولى. والمراد بالتفريق أن يحكم القاضي بالتفريق بينهما كما في العناية وفي الجوهرة وغاية البيان لو فرق بينهما ثم وطئها وجب الحد عليه. وينبغي أن يقيده بما إذا وطئها بعد انقضاء العدة وإلا فوطء المعتدة لا الحد. وجعل في التتمة قول زفر قول أبي القاسم الصفار البلخي وأن الإمام أبا بكر البلخي يقول من وقت الفرقة. وفي البزازية في النكاح الفاسد: لا تعتد في بيت الزوج. وفي زمانا ثم يوجب قال لها كنت طلقتك منذ كذا وهي لا تعلم بذلك يصدق وتعتبر عدتها من ذلك الوقت ثم لا تجب عليه نفقة ولا سكنى لاعترافها بالسقوط، وعلى قول هؤلاء ينبغي أن لا يحل له التزوج بأختها وأربع سواها قوله: (تعتبر العدة من يوم الشهادة لا من يوم القضاء) قال بعض الفضلاء: هذا على حذف مضاف أي من يوم تحمل الشهادة لا من يوم أدائها فإنهما لو شهدا في المحرم أنه طلقها في شوال كان ابتداء العدة من His saying: (And in the invalid marriage after separation or determination to abstain from intercourse) i.e., the start of the 'iddah. And Zufar said: From the last of the intercourses because intercourse is the cause that obligates it. And our proof: that every intercourse that occurs in the invalid marriage is treated like a single act because all depend on the ruling of one contract, and for this reason one mahr suffices for all. So before mutaraka (separation) or determination, the 'iddah is not established with the possibility of another intercourse. And because the possibility due to doubt is treated as the reality of intercourse due to its hidden nature and the need to know the ruling with respect to others. And in al-Khulasa: Mutaraka in invalid marriage after consummation is only by words, like his saying "I leave you" or what stands in its place like "I leave her" or "I set her free". As for absence, it is not mutaraka because if he returns, it resumes. And if he denies the marriage, it is not mutaraka. And we have preceded in invalid marriage that if they differ regarding consummation, his word is accepted regarding the mahr, so the mahr is not obligatory, and that the intended 'iddah is the 'iddah of mutaraka, so there is no 'iddah upon his death except after consummation, and that there is no mourning (ihdad) and no maintenance (nafaqah) in it. And if he marries the sister of his wife in an invalid marriage, she is forbidden to him until the completion of her 'iddah. And that its obligation is only in judgment (qada), but as a matter of conscience (diyana), if she knows that she has menstruated three times after the last intercourse, it becomes lawful for her to marry without separation and the like. And that divorce in it is mutaraka. And that denial of the marriage if it is in her presence is mutaraka, otherwise not. And that knowledge of the other about mutaraka is a condition according to one opinion and it is sahih (correct), and it was said no and it is sahih, and we have preferred the second. And that mutaraka is not specific to the husband, but can also be from the woman. Therefore Miskin mentioned in his commentary among its forms that she says to him: "I leave you", and we have preceded many of its rulings there, so refer to it. And from what we have established, it is known that mere determination is not sufficient, but rather there must be an announcement indicating it. Therefore al-ʿInayah said: Determination is an inner matter not known, and it has an outward indication which is the announcement. So if he said, as in al-Islah, or showing his determination, it is better. And what is meant by separation is that the judge rules for separation between them, as in al-ʿInayah. And in al-Jawhara and Ghayat al-Bayan: If he separated them then he had intercourse with her, the hadd penalty is obligatory upon him. And it should be restricted to when he had intercourse with her after the completion of the 'iddah, otherwise the intercourse of a woman in 'iddah does not require hadd. And he made in al-Tatimmah the statement of Zufar the statement of Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar al-Balkhi, and that Imam Abu Bakr al-Balkhi says from the time of separation. And in al-Bazzaziyya regarding invalid marriage: She does not observe 'iddah in the husband's house. And when time passes then it obligates: He said to her: I divorced you such-and-such time ago, while she does not know that. He is believed, and her 'iddah is considered from that time, then no maintenance or housing is obligatory upon him due to her acknowledgment of its fall. And according to these, it should be that he is not permitted to marry her sister or four others besides her. His saying: (The 'iddah is considered from the day of testimony, not from the day of judgment) Some scholars said: This is with the deletion of a genitive, i.e., from the day of bearing the testimony, not from the day of performing it. For if they testify in Muharram that he divorced her in Shawwal, the beginning of the 'iddah is from Shawwal, as will come. His saying: (And therefore Miskin mentioned etc.) He said in al-Nahr: We have preceded what refutes it, i.e., in the chapter on mahr in invalid marriage, and we have preceded the discussion on that there. His saying: (And it should be restricted etc.) This is contrary to the apparent, because the obligation of hadd
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage focuses on the start of the 'iddah in an invalid marriage (nikah fasid) and the conditions for mutaraka (separation). The passage type is intra-Hanafi dispute, as it again contrasts the Hanafi majority with Zufar. Zufar holds that the 'iddah begins from the last intercourse because intercourse is the causative factor. The Hanafi position, however, treats all acts of intercourse in an invalid marriage as a single unit under one contract, so the 'iddah begins only after separation (mutaraka) or a firm determination to abstain. Before that, the possibility of further intercourse prevents the 'iddah from commencing. The text then details the conditions for mutaraka: it must be by explicit words (e.g., 'I leave you'), not merely by absence or denial of the marriage. It also covers that the 'iddah in an invalid marriage is the 'iddah of mutaraka (not of death), with no mourning (ihdad) or maintenance (nafaqah). The obligation holds in judicial (qada) terms but not in conscience (diyana) if the woman knows her cycles are complete after the last intercourse. The passage also discusses that divorce in such a marriage constitutes mutaraka, and that knowledge of the other party is a condition according to some. The author emphasizes that mere determination (ʿazm) is insufficient; one must announce the intention. The final part clarifies that the phrase 'from the day of testimony' refers to the day the event occurred, not the court proceeding. The text ends abruptly, but establishes the key ruling that the 'iddah in invalid marriage is tied to separation, not to the last intercourse.

Key Terms
متاركة (mutārakah): Separation in an invalid marriage by explicit words indicating cessation of the marriage.
الوطء (al-waṭʾ): Sexual intercourse; in invalid marriage, all acts are treated as one.
نكاح فاسد (nikāḥ fāsid): A marriage that is defective in its contract but not void; it has some legal effects like 'iddah and barring of marriage to relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what triggers the beginning of 'iddah in an invalid marriage?
A) The last act of intercourse.
B) The judge's ruling of separation.
C) The husband's determination to abstain or explicit separation (mutaraka).
D) The wife's claim that she is pregnant.

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah in an invalid marriage begins only after formal separation (mutaraka) or a definite intention to abstain, because all intercourses are considered a single act under one contract.

Rulings on Mahr and 'Iddah When a Fasid Marriage Precedes a Valid Marriage
Rulings on marriage in 'iddah after fasid versus sahih marriages with reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on mahr and 'iddah when a fasid marriage is followed by a valid marriage in the 'iddah period, and distinguish the outcome when the order is reversed.

Core Idea
A fasid marriage does not legally transfer consummation to a subsequent valid marriage for mahr and 'iddah purposes.

This lesson examines the second of four scenarios presented in the text regarding marriages that occur during the 'iddah period. It focuses on the situation where a fasid marriage is consummated, then a valid marriage is contracted while the wife is still in the 'iddah from the fasid marriage. The text also provides the reverse scenario and the underlying reasoning based on the inability to consummate in fasid marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sequences
Note the two possible orders: fasid first then valid, and valid first then fasid. Understand that the ruling on mahr and 'iddah differs.
The fasid-first sequence is the primary scenario; the reverse is given as a contrast.
2
Determine the ruling for fasid-first
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two), full mahr is wajib and a fresh 'iddah is required when the valid marriage is divorced before consummation.
This is stated as 'عندهما'.
3
Determine the ruling for the reverse sequence
When the valid marriage comes first and the fasid marriage occurs during its 'iddah, no mahr and no fresh 'iddah; she completes the first 'iddah by agreement.
The reasoning is that the husband cannot legally consummate the fasid marriage.
4
Understand the rationale
In the reverse scenario, the husand is not considered a cohabiter in the fasid marriage due to actual impossibility, so no legal effects arise. In the fasid-first scenario, the fasid consummation does not enter the valid marriage, yet full mahr is due according to the two.
The text does not fully explain the fasid-first ruling; it is given as is.
5
Note the third scenario
The third scenario briefly states that if consummation occurs in a valid marriage, the 'iddah for a slave woman is two menstruations from the time of purchase.
This is a separate case about 'iddah duration for a slave wife.

Source Text

ثانيها لو تزوجها نكاحاً فاسداً ودخل بها ففرق بينهما ثم تزوجها صحيحاً وهي في العدة عن ذلك الفاسد ثم طلقها قبل الدخول يجب عليه مهر كامل وعليها عدة مستقبلة عندهما. ولو كان على القلب بأن تزوجها أولاً صحيحاً ثم طلقها بعد الدخول ثم تزوجها في العدة فاسداً لا يجب عليه مهر ولا عليها عدة مستقبلة ويجب عليها اتمام العدة الأولى بالاتفاق. والفرق لهما أنه لا يتمكن من الوطء الفاسد فلا يجعل واطئاً حكماً لعدم الإمكان حقيقة ولهذا لا يجعل واطئاً بالخلوة في الفاسد حتى لا تجب العدة بها ولا عليه المهر. وثالثها أنه لو دخل بها في الصحة عدة النكاح وهي حيضتان من وقت الشراء. ورابعها لو تزوجت بغير كفء ودخل بها ففرق القاضي بينهما بطلب الولي ثم تزوجها هذا الرجل في العدة بمهر وفرق القاضي بينهما قبل أن يدخل بها كان عليه المهر الثاني كاملاً وعدة مستقبلة عندهما استحساناً، وعند محمد نصف المهر الثاني وعليها تمام العدة الأولى.
Second: If he married her with a fasid (invalid) marriage and consummated, then they were separated, then he married her validly while she was in 'iddah from that fasid marriage, then divorced her before consummation: a full mahr is obligatory and a fresh 'iddah is upon her according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And if it were the reverse: that he first married her validly, then divorced her after consummation, then married her in 'iddah invalidly: no mahr is obligatory and no fresh 'iddah upon her, and she must complete the first 'iddah by agreement. The difference for them is that he does not have the ability to have intercourse in the invalid marriage, so he is not legally considered a cohabiter due to actual impossibility, and therefore he is not considered a cohabiter by seclusion in the invalid marriage, so 'iddah is not required nor mahr. Third: that if he consummated in the valid marriage, the 'iddah of marriage is two menstruations from the time of purchase. Fourth: If she married a non-kufu and consummated, then the judge separated them at the guardian's request, then this man married her in 'iddah with a mahr, and the judge separated them before he consummated: then the second full mahr is upon him and a fresh 'iddah according to the two by istihsan, while according to Muhammad, half the second mahr and she must complete the first 'iddah.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage contains three distinct rulings (thani, thalith, rabi) that further illustrate the principle of whether consummation in the first marriage legally enters the second. The second ruling: If a man marries a woman invalidly (fasid) and consummates, then they are separated, then he marries her validly while she is in 'iddah from the fasid marriage, then divorces her before consummation in the valid marriage: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, he must pay a full mahr and she must observe a fresh 'iddah. The reasoning is that the fasid marriage's consummation does not legally count for the valid marriage because the fasid marriage itself is invalid and the husband is not considered a cohabiter in a legal sense (he did not have the ability to have legitimate intercourse). However, if the order is reversed (valid first, then fasid in 'iddah), then no mahr and no fresh 'iddah; she completes the first 'iddah, unanimously. The third ruling is fragmentary but seems to state that if he consummated in the valid marriage, the 'iddah from that marriage is two menstruations from the time of purchase (this might be about a slave woman?). The fourth ruling concerns a woman who married someone not her kufu (social equivalent), the judge separated them, then the same man married her in her 'iddah with a mahr but the judge separated them before consummation. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the second mahr is fully payable and a fresh 'iddah is required (by istihsan), while Muhammad says only half the second mahr and she completes the first 'iddah. This again hinges on whether the first marriage's consummation enters the second: for the two, the first valid consummation makes the second marriage's divorce after consummation (hence full mahr), while Muhammad considers the first valid consummation not counting for the second marriage, so only half mahr.

Key Terms
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage due to a defect that can be rectified (e.g., missing witness), but not batil (void ab initio).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second scenario, when a fasid marriage is consummated and then a valid marriage occurs during its 'iddah and divorce before consummation, what is the ruling on mahr according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
A) No mahr
B) Half mahr
C) Full mahr
D) Double mahr

Key Takeaway
The order of marriages and the consummation of the first determine mahr and 'iddah obligations in Hanafi law.

Nikah — Marriage

Rulings on Mahr and 'Iddah When a Woman Marries a Non-Kufu and Then Remarries in the 'Iddah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr and 'iddah when a non-kufu marriage annulled and remarriage in 'iddah is annulled before consummation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on mahr and 'iddah when a woman marries a non-kufu, is separated, and then the same man marries her again during her 'iddah, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the mahr amount.

Core Idea
When a non-kufu marriage is annulled, a subsequent marriage in 'iddah triggers full mahr and fresh 'iddah according to the two by istihsan, but half mahr and completion of first 'iddah according to Muhammad.

This lesson examines the fourth scenario from the text, which involves a marriage to a non-kufu (someone not socially equivalent) that is annulled by the judge, followed by a remarriage during the 'iddah period. The ruling presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Muhammad, with the two using istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Understand the factual sequence
A woman marries a man who is not her kufu, consummates, the judge annuls at the guardian's request. Then the same man marries her again during her 'iddah with a mahr, but the judge annuls before consummation in the second marriage.
Key point: the second marriage is annulled before consummation.
2
Note the ruling of the two
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the husband must pay the full second mahr and she must observe a fresh 'iddah. They base this on istihsan.
Istihsan is a juristic preference overriding qiyas.
3
Note Muhammad's ruling
Imam Muhammad holds that the husband pays only half the second mahr and she completes the first 'iddah (from the non-kufu marriage).
This is a strict application of qiyas: divorce before consummation gives half mahr.
4
Analyze the basis of ikhtilaf
The ikhtilaf centers on whether the consummation of the first (non-kufu) marriage legally enters the second marriage. The two say yes by istihsan; Muhammad says no, each marriage is independent.
The difference determines both the mahr amount and which 'iddah applies.
5
Determine the practical difference
The husband pays either full or half mahr; the wife either starts a new 'iddah or completes the first one. This has financial and legal implications.
The mufta bihi is likely the two's view as it is majority and based on istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيها لو تزوجها نكاحاً فاسداً ودخل بها ففرق بينهما ثم تزوجها صحيحاً وهي في العدة عن ذلك الفاسد ثم طلقها قبل الدخول يجب عليه مهر كامل وعليها عدة مستقبلة عندهما. ولو كان على القلب بأن تزوجها أولاً صحيحاً ثم طلقها بعد الدخول ثم تزوجها في العدة فاسداً لا يجب عليه مهر ولا عليها عدة مستقبلة ويجب عليها اتمام العدة الأولى بالاتفاق. والفرق لهما أنه لا يتمكن من الوطء الفاسد فلا يجعل واطئاً حكماً لعدم الإمكان حقيقة ولهذا لا يجعل واطئاً بالخلوة في الفاسد حتى لا تجب العدة بها ولا عليه المهر. وثالثها أنه لو دخل بها في الصحة عدة النكاح وهي حيضتان من وقت الشراء. ورابعها لو تزوجت بغير كفء ودخل بها ففرق القاضي بينهما بطلب الولي ثم تزوجها هذا الرجل في العدة بمهر وفرق القاضي بينهما قبل أن يدخل بها كان عليه المهر الثاني كاملاً وعدة مستقبلة عندهما استحساناً، وعند محمد نصف المهر الثاني وعليها تمام العدة الأولى.
Second: If he married her with a fasid (invalid) marriage and consummated, then they were separated, then he married her validly while she was in 'iddah from that fasid marriage, then divorced her before consummation: a full mahr is obligatory and a fresh 'iddah is upon her according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Commentary
This passage contains three distinct rulings (thani, thalith, rabi) that further illustrate the principle of whether consummation in the first marriage legally enters the second. The second ruling: If a man marries a woman invalidly (fasid) and consummates, then they are separated, then he marries her validly while she is in 'iddah from the fasid marriage, then divorces her before consummation in the valid marriage: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, he must pay a full mahr and she must observe a fresh 'iddah. The reasoning is that the fasid marriage's consummation does not legally count for the valid marriage because the fasid marriage itself is invalid and the husband is not considered a cohabiter in a legal sense (he did not have the ability to have legitimate intercourse). However, if the order is reversed (valid first, then fasid in 'iddah), then no mahr and no fresh 'iddah; she completes the first 'iddah, unanimously. The third ruling is fragmentary but seems to state that if he consummated in the valid marriage, the 'iddah from that marriage is two menstruations from the time of purchase (this might be about a slave woman?). Key Terms
كفء (kufu): Social and religious equivalence between spouses (e.g., lineage, wealth, piety) required for valid marriage.
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage due to a defect that can be rectified (e.g., missing witness), but not batil (void ab initio).

A) Full mahr
B) Half mahr
C) No mahr
D) Double mahr

Key Takeaway
Istihsan can override qiyas in Hanafi law, leading to full mahr even when the second marriage is annulled before consummation.

Nikah — Marriage

Establishing Paternity through Marriage and Midwife Testimony
Ruling on establishing paternity for a married woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two ways paternity is established for a married woman and explain the role of the midwife's testimony in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Paternity is established by marriage (firash); the midwife's testimony only removes suspicion, it does not create lineage.

How is a child's paternity determined in Hanafi law? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the foundational rule: a child born to a married woman at least six months after marriage is attributed to the husband if he remains silent. If he denies, a midwife's testimony can confirm the birth. But what is the legal function of that testimony? We will explore the principle of 'firash' and the significance of the midwife's role in removing suspicion (tuhma).

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Find the core statement: 'The married woman (al-mankūḥa) after six months, if he is silent, and if he denies, then by the testimony of a woman on the birth.' Recognize that this is the primary ruling of the chapter.
The six-month minimum is derived from the shortest possible gestation period in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the role of silence (sukūt)
Note that silence without acknowledgment or denial is sufficient to establish paternity. This is because the marriage bed (firash) is the basis, and silence implies consent.
If the husband explicitly denies, he must undergo li‘an to negate paternity.
3
Analyze the function of midwife testimony
The commentary clarifies that the midwife's testimony does not establish lineage itself (since that is already done by the firash) but rather identifies the child and removes suspicion (tuhma) from the woman. This is analogous to an oath in legal proceedings.
This distinction is crucial: the testimony affirms the birth event, not the paternity.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
Abu Hanifa requires stronger evidence (two men or one man and two women) when the pregnancy was not apparent or the husband did not acknowledge it. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept one free Muslim woman's testimony unconditionally.
This dispute affects whether a single midwife's testimony is sufficient in all cases or only when certain conditions are met.
5
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, if a divorced woman without apparent pregnancy gives birth and the husband denies, her testimony alone does not bind him; under the Sahibayn, it does, and the child inherits. The later fatwa prefers the view that facilitates the child's rights.
The mufta bihi position leans toward the Sahibayn's view in most contemporary cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب ثبوت النسب
أشهر فصاعداً إن سكت وإن جحد فبشهادة امرأة على الولادة فإن ولدت ثم اختلفا
بندار أنه بعد الثبوت بقيت مؤتمنة فكان القول قولها إلا أن القابلة جعلت شرطاً للعادة لأنها لا تلد إلا بالقابلة وإني أقول: إن القابلة شرط زوال التهمة كاليمين في رد الوديعة واليمين في دعوى انقضاء العدة، فإذا لم تشهد قابلة بقيت متهمة فلا يقبل قولها فيه اهـ كلامه. وهو يصلح توفيقاً لكلامهم فمن نفي اشتراط شهادة القابلة أفاد أنها ليست شرطاً حقيقة لثبوت النسب، ومن أثبته أراد به أنها شرط لزوال التهمة عن نفسها وهو كلام حسن يجب قبوله. وأفاد بقوله «شهادة رجلين» قبول شهادة الرجال على الولادة من الأجنبية وأنهم لا يفسقون بالنظر إلى عورتها إما لكونه قد يتفق ذلك من غير قصد نظر ولا تعمد أو لضرورة كما في شهود الزنا، ولا يخفى أنها إذا ولدت وجحد الزوج ولادتها وادعت أن حبلها كان ظاهراً وأنكر ظهوره فلا بد من إقامة البينة عليه إما رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، فظهور الحبل عند الإنكار إنما يكون بإقامة البينة لأن الحبل وقت المنازعة لم يكن موجوداً حتى يكفي ظهوره لأنها بعد الولادة ولم أر من صرح به قوله: (والمنكوحة لستة أشهر فصاعداً إن سكت وإن جحد بشهادة امرأة على الولادة) أي يثبت نسب ولد المنكوحة حقيقة إذا جاءت به لستة أشهر أو أكثر من وقت التزوج بأحد الشيئين: إما بالسكوت من غير اعتراف ولا نفي له، وإما بشهادة القابلة عند إنكار الولادة لأن الفراش قائم والمدة تامة فوجب القول بثبوته، اعترف به
إلزامه ولد غيره اهـ قوله: (وهو يصلح توفيقاً لكلامهم) الخ قال في النهر: للبحث فيه مجال فتدبره اهـ. وقال المقدسي في شرحه وأقول: هذا التوفيق بعيد عن التحقيق لأن الاشتراط إنما يكون لترتيب الأحكام الظاهرة، أما مجرد زوال التهمة فلا ثمرة له. اهـ. أقول والأظهر أنهما قولان متغايران والذي قاله في التبيين هو الذي يدل عليه كلام الهداية أخراً، وكذا كلام الاختيار وصرح به في الجوهرة. وقال المصنف في الكافي عند تقرير دليل الإمام: بخلاف ما لو أقر الزوج بالحبل أو كان الحبل ظاهراً فإن النسب ثابت قبل الولادة والحاجة إلى تعيينه لأن الخصم يقول لعله هلك فخرج ميتاً أو مات بعد الخروج فلم يكن بد من تعيينه والتعيين يثبت بشهادة القابلة. اهـ. فقوله والتعيين يثبت بشهادة القابلة صريح في أن ظهوره أو الإقرار به لا يفيد تعيينه بدون شهادة القابلة وعلى هذا مشى المحقق ابن كمال والمحقق ابن الهمام وفي كافي الحاكم الشهيد وإن جحدت الورثة أن تكون هي يقبل على الولادة شهادة امرأة واحدة إذا لم يكن حبلاً ظاهراً أو لم يكن الزوج أقر به في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد تقبل شهادة المرأة الواحدة إذا كانت حرة مسلمة ويثبت النسب وله الميراث، ولو كان الزوج أقر بالحبل ثم جاءت به لسنتين بعد موته وشهدت على ولادتها امرأة مسلمة حرة جازت شهادتها، وكذلك لو كان حبلاً ظاهراً. قال أبو الفضل معنى قوله «ثم جاءت به لسنتين بعد موته» أنها جاءت بعد موته لسنتين من وقت إخباره رجل طلق ثلاثاً أو طلاقاً بائناً فجاءت بولد بعد الطلاق لسنتين أو أقل وجاءت بامرأة تشهد على الولادة والزوج منكر للولد والحبل البحر الرائق/ ج ٤ / م ١٨
ولدته لم
فقالت نكحتني منذ ستة أشهر وادعى الأقل فالقول لها وهو ابنه ولو علق طلاقها
أنه
أو سكت أو أنكر ، حتى لو نفاه لا ينتفي إلا باللعان. وفي التحقيق شهادة القابلة لم يثبت بها النسب لأنه ثابت بقيام الفراش وإنما يثبت بها تعيين الولد. قيد بستة أشهر لأنها لو ولدته لأقل منها لم يثبت نسبه لأن العلوق سابق على النكاح فلا يكون منه، ويفسد النكاح لاحتمال من زوج آخر بنكاح صحيح أو بشبهة، وأفاد أنها لو جاءت به لتمام ستة أشهر بلا زيادة أنها كالأكثر. قالوا: لاحتمال أنه تزوجها واطئاً لها فوافق الإنزال النكاح والنسب يحتاط في إثباته. ويرد عليه ما تقدم في المبتوتة حيث نفى نسب ما أتت به لتمام سنتين مع تصحيحه بأنه طلقها حال جماعها وصادف الإنزال الطلاق وأجيب عنه بأن ثبوت النسب هنا لحمل أمرها على الصلاح إذ لو لم يثبت هنا لزم كونه من زنا أو من زوج فتزوجت به وهي في العدة، وأما عدم الثبوت هناك للشك فلا يستلزم نسبه فساد إليها لجواز كون عدتها قد انقضت وتزوجت بزوج آخر فعلقت منه. أطلق المصنف في المرأة هنا وقيدها في الشهادات بالعدالة، وقيدها في المبسوط بالحرية والإسلام ولم يشترط العدالة والظاهر الأول. وفي الولوالجية: رجل تزوج بامرأة فجاءت بسقط قد استبان خلفه، فإن جاءت به لأربعة أشهر جاز النكاح ويثبت النسب من الزوج الثاني، وإن جاءت به الأربعة أشهر إلا يوماً لم يجز لأن في الوجه الأول الولد للزوج الثاني، وفي الوجه الثاني من الزوج الأول لأن خلقه
النكاح لا يستبين إلا في مائة وعشرين يوما فيكون أربعين يوماً نطفة وأربعين علقة وأربعين مضغة اهـ. قوله: (فإن ولدت ثم اختلفا فقالت نكحتني منذ ستة أشهر وادعى الأقل فالقول لها وهو ابنه) لأن الظاهر شاهد لها فإنها تدل ظاهراً من نكاح لا من سفاح ولا من زوج تزوجت بهذا الزوج في عدته وهو مقدم على الظاهر الذي يشهد له وهو إضافة الحادث وهو النكاح إلى أقرب الأوقات لأنه إذا تعارض ظاهران في ثبوت نسب قدم المثبت له لوجوب الاحتياط فيه حتى إنه يثبت بالإيماء مع القدرة على النطق بخلاف سائر التصرفات مع أن ظاهرها متأيد لم يلزمه النسب حتى يشهد رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان في قول أبي حنيفة، ويلزمه النسب في قولهما بشهادة المرأة، وسواء كانت هذه المعتدة حرة مسلمة أو كتابية أو أمة في هذا الحكم اهـ. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان وكذا المبتوتة والمطلقة طلاقاً رجعياً إذا ادعت الولادة عند أبي حنيفة لا تثبت الولادة بشهادة القابلة إلا إذا كان الحبل ظاهراً أو كان الزوج أقر بالحبل.
قوله: ( وادعت أن حبلها كان ظاهراً) لم يبين ما يكون به الحبل ظاهراً. وفي الشرنبلالية: وظهور الحبل أن تأتي به لأقل من ستة أشهر كما في السراج. وقال الشيخ قاسم: المراد بظهور الحبل أن تكون أمارات حملها بالغة مبلغاً يوجب غلبة الظن بكونها حاملاً لكل من شاهدها ا هـ قوله: (لأنه لا يلزم من تزوجها حاملاً اثبات النسب الخ) عبارة الفتح: لأنه لا يلزم منه تزوجها حاملاً بثابث
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Establishing Lineage. For [the married woman] after six months if he is silent, and if he denies then by the testimony of a woman on the birth. Then if she gives birth and they dispute... Bandar said that after establishment she remains trustworthy, so her word is accepted, except that the midwife is made a condition for the custom because she does not give birth except with a midwife. I say: the midwife is a condition for removing suspicion, like the oath in returning the deposit and the oath in the claim of expiry of the waiting period. So if a midwife does not testify, she remains suspect and her word is not accepted... And his statement that the testimony of two men is accepted for birth from a non-mahram woman, and they are not corrupted by looking at her private parts either because it may happen without intention or due to necessity as in witnesses of adultery... And it is not hidden that if she gives birth and the husband denies her birth and she claims her pregnancy was apparent and he denies its appearance, then evidence must be established, either two men or one man and two women... And his statement: (The married woman after six months if he is silent, and if he denies then by the testimony of a woman on the birth) i.e., the lineage of the child of the married woman is truly established if she brings him after six months or more from the time of marriage by one of two things: either by silence without acknowledgment or denial, or by the testimony of the midwife at the denial of birth because the marriage bed is established and the period is complete...
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of establishing lineage (thubut al-nasab) from a Hanafi fiqh work. It begins with a ruling: the paternity of a child born to a married woman is established if she gives birth at least six months after marriage, provided the husband remains silent (acknowledging the child) or, if he denies, a midwife testifies to the birth. The commentary clarifies that the midwife's testimony is not a condition for establishing lineage itself—since lineage is already established by the marriage (firash)—but rather a condition to remove suspicion (tuhma) from the woman. This is analogous to the oath in cases of returning a deposit or claiming the end of the waiting period. The author then discusses intra-madhhab differences between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the acceptance of a single woman's testimony on birth in certain cases. Abu Hanifa requires two men or one man and two women when the pregnancy was not apparent or the husband did not acknowledge it, while the two disciples accept one free Muslim woman's testimony. The passage also addresses disputes after birth: if the wife claims she married six months ago and the husband claims less, her word is accepted and the child is his. The commentary emphasizes that lineage is established with caution (ihtiyat) and that the default is to attribute the child to the marriage. It also touches on the case of a divorced woman (mubtatta) and the requirement of a midwife's testimony when the pregnancy was not apparent. A separate case of a miscarriage at four months is discussed, where the child is attributed to the second husband if born at four months, but to the first if earlier. Overall, the passage presents the Hanafi position on establishing paternity through marriage, silence, testimony, and careful consideration of timelines.

Key Terms
القابلة (al-qābilah): The midwife who assists at birth; her testimony is accepted to confirm the birth and identify the child.
الفراش (al-firāsh): The marriage relationship that serves as the basis for attributing a child to the husband; 'the child belongs to the bed'.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion of wrongdoing; the midwife's testimony removes suspicion from the woman regarding the birth.
المبتوتة (al-mubtattah): A woman irrevocably divorced (ba'in); her rulings on lineage differ from a revocably divorced woman.
اللعان (al-li‘ān): Mutual imprecation; the only way to negate paternity when the husband accuses the wife of adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary basis for establishing a child's paternity to a married woman?
A) The testimony of a midwife.
B) The husband's explicit acknowledgment.
C) The existence of a valid marriage (firash).
D) The birth of the child at full term.

Key Takeaway
Paternity is established by the marriage (firash) if the child is born at least six months after marriage; the husband's silence or a midwife's testimony serves as evidence of the birth, not the cause of lineage.

Maintenance Amount: Husband's Status vs Both Spouses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on basis of maintenance amount.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the basis for maintenance amount, explain the tarjih mechanism, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi considers both spouses' status and gives the middle amount; the surplus is a debt.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: should maintenance (nafaqah) be determined solely by the husband's financial status or by considering both spouses' circumstances? The answer directly affects the wife's entitlement when spouses have unequal wealth. We will trace the two positions, their proofs from Quran and Hadith, and how later authorities resolved the conflict to establish the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, understand the two views: (1) Zahir al-riwayah: only the husband's status matters. (2) Mufta bihi: both spouses' statuses matter, leading to the middle amount (nafaqat al-wast).
The passage explicitly contrasts these.
2
Locate the key scholars
Al-Karkhi and Muhammad al-Shaybani represent the first view; al-Khassaf and the author of al-Hidayah represent the second, which is the relied-upon fatwa.
This shows the school's evolution across generations.
3
Examine the proofs
The first view relies on Quran 65:7 (spending according to capacity). The second view adds the hadith of Hind and resolves the apparent conflict by making the surplus a debt on the husband.
The mufta bihi does not abandon the verse; it implements it via debt.
4
Understand the tarjih resolution
The middle amount is obligatory immediately; the difference between it and the wealthy maintenance becomes a debt, due when the husband becomes able. This was the reasoning in al-Hidayah.
This addresses the objection of overburdening a poor husband.
5
Note the practical difference and sub-rule
When spouses disagree about wealth, the husband's claim is accepted unless the wife proves otherwise. This procedural rule complements the substantive ruling.
Important for the mufti handling disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحسب عرف تلك البلدة ويقوم الأصناف بالدراهم ثم يقدر بالدراهم كما في المحيط، أما باعتبار حاله أو باعتبار حالهما، واختار المصنف الثاني وهو قول الخصاف، وفي الهداية وعليه الفتوى، وفي الولوالجية وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى وظاهر الرواية اعتبار حاله فقط وهو قول الكرخي وبه قال جمع كثير من المشايخ ونص عليه محمد وقال في التحفة والبدائع : إنه الصحيح نظراً إلى قوله تعالى لينفق ذو سعة من سعته ومن قدر عليه رزقه فلينفق مما آتاه الله لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا ما أتاها [الطلاق ] واستدل في الهداية لاعتبار حالهما بحديث هند فإنه اعتبر حالهما، وأما النص فنقول بموجبه إنه مخاطب بقدر وسعه والباقي دين في ذمته. وحاصله أنه عمل بالآية والحديث واتفقوا على وجوب نفقة الموسرين إذا كانا موسرين، وعلى نفقة المعسرين إذا كانا معسرين وإنما الاختلاف فيما إذا كان أحدهما موسراً والآخر معسراً فعلى ظاهر الرواية الاعتبار لحال الرجل؛ فإن كان موسراً وهي معسرة تجب عليه نفقة الموسرين ولا يجب عليه أن يطعمها مما يأكل لكن قال مشايخنا : يستحب له أن يؤاكلها لأنه مأمور بحسن العشرة معها وذا في أن يؤاكلها لتكون نفقتها ونفقته سواء، وإن كان معسراً وهي موسرة وجب عليه نفقة المعسرين لأنها لما تزوجت معسراً فقد رضيت بنفقة المعسرين، وأما على المفتى به فتجب نفقة الوسط في المسألتين وهي فوق نفقة المعسرة ودون نفقة الموسرة، فإذا كان الزوج مفرطا في اليسار يأكل الحلواء واللحم المشوي والباجات والمرأة فقيرة تأكل في بيتها خبز الشعير لا يجب عليه أن يطعمها مما يأكل في بيته بنفسه ولا ما كانت تأكل في بيت أهلها ولكن يطعمها الوسط وهو خبز البر وباجة أو باجتين؛ كذا في الذخيرة . وفي غاية البيان إنه إذا كان معسراً وهي موسرة وأوجبنا الوسط فقد كلفناه بما ليس في وسعه فلا يجوز وهو غفلة عما في الهداية كما قدمناه من أنه مخاطب بقدر وسعه والباقي دين إلى الميسرة فليس تكليفاً بما ليس في وسعه. قوله: (وإن كان معسراً وهي موسرة الخ) قال الرملي : فلو اختلفا فادعى الإعسار وهي الإيسار قال في الخانية في باب النفقة : فإن قال الرجل أنا وعلى نفقة المعسرين كان القول قوله إلا أن تقيم المرأة البينة .
According to the custom of that town, he estimates the types (of food) in dirhams and then estimates in dirhams, as in al-Muhit. Either considering his status or considering both statuses. The author chose the second, which is the saying of al-Khassaf. In al-Hidayah: 'And upon it is the fatwa.' In al-Walwaljiyyah: 'It is the correct view and upon it is the fatwa.' The apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) is considering only his status, which is the saying of al-Karkhi, and many shaykhs agreed with him, and Muhammad explicitly stated it. In al-Tuhfah and al-Bada'i': 'It is the correct view, because of the verse (65:7).' In al-Hidayah, he used the hadith of Hind as proof for considering both statuses. As for the verse, we say according to its implication: he is addressed within his capacity, and the remainder is a debt in his liability. The summary is that he acted upon both the verse and the hadith. They agreed on the obligation of maintenance of the wealthy when both are wealthy, and of the poor when both are poor. The difference is only when one is wealthy and the other poor. According to the apparent transmission, consideration is given to the man's status: if he is wealthy and she is poor, the maintenance of the wealthy is obligatory upon him, and he is not obliged to feed her from what he eats, but our shaykhs said: it is recommended for him to eat with her because he is commanded to treat her well, and that is that he should eat with her so that her maintenance and his are the same. If he is poor and she is wealthy, the maintenance of the poor is obligatory upon him because when she married a poor man, she consented to the maintenance of the poor. According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi), the middle maintenance is obligatory in both cases, which is above the poor maintenance and below the wealthy maintenance. So if the husband is extremely wealthy, eating halwa, grilled meat, and pastries, and the wife is poor, eating barley bread in her house, he is not obliged to feed her from what he eats in his own house nor from what she used to eat in her family's house, but he feeds her the middle: wheat bread and one or two pastries. So in al-Dhakhirah. In Ghayat al-Bayan: If he is poor and she is wealthy and we impose the middle, we have charged him with what is beyond his capacity, so it is not permissible. This is negligence of what is in al-Hidayah, as we presented: 'He is addressed within his capacity, and the remainder is a debt until ease.' So it is not a charge beyond his capacity. He said: (And if he is poor and she is wealthy, etc.) al-Ramli said: If they disagree, he claiming poverty and she claiming wealth, in al-Khaniyyah in the chapter of maintenance: If the man says, 'I am upon the maintenance of the poor,' his word is accepted unless the woman brings proof.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the basis for determining the amount of spousal maintenance. The core issue: should we look only at the husband's financial status, or at the status of both spouses? The author presents the positions. Zahir al-Riwayah (the primary transmitted position) considers only the husband's status, as stated by al-Karkhi and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The author of al-Hidayah and later fatwas prefer considering both statuses and giving the middle amount when they differ. The Quranic verse (65:7) is cited by those who consider only the husband's capacity, while the hadith of Hind is used to support considering the wife's needs. The resolution offered is that the husband is only required to pay within his immediate capacity, but any shortfall remains a debt on him, so the middle amount does not exceed his eventual ability. The passage also includes a sub-rule: if the husband and wife disagree about their financial status, the husband's claim is accepted unless the wife proves otherwise.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent transmission from the early Hanafi authorities (the six books of Muhammad al-Shaybani) indicating that maintenance is based solely on the husband's status.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon position for fatwa, which in this case is the middle amount considering both spouses' status.
نفقة الوسط (nafaqat al-wast): The middle level of maintenance, between the wealthy and poor amounts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Maintenance of the wealthy (nafaqat al-musirin)
B) Maintenance of the poor (nafaqat al-mu'sirin)
C) Middle maintenance (nafaqat al-wast)
D) The amount the wife used to eat in her father's house

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in Hanafi law is the middle maintenance when spouses' statuses differ, with the surplus being a debt.

Condition of Provisioning (Tawmin) in Marriage Contract Not Binding
Ruling that a condition in marriage contract to provide maintenance as provisions (tawmin) without estimation is not binding, and the wife can demand estimation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a condition in the marriage contract to provide maintenance as provisions without estimation, and apply the principle that such a condition is not binding.

Core Idea
A condition in the marriage contract to provide unspecified provisions is not binding; the wife may demand estimation.

In this lesson, we examine a specific condition in the marriage contract: maintenance as provisions (tawmin) without a fixed monetary estimation. The Hanafi school rules that such a condition is not binding, meaning the wife retains the right to request a formal estimate. We also explore a procedural issue between Hanafi and Shafi'i judges regarding the finality of a maintenance judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the marriage contract includes a condition that maintenance be provided as provisions (tawmin) without a quantified estimate.
The wife seeks to later demand a specific estimation.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The condition is not binding (ghayr lazim). The wife has the right to request a formal estimation of maintenance.
This is based on legal principles, as stated in the text.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
The condition lacks a definite amount, making it unenforceable. The purpose of maintenance is to provide for the wife's needs, which require certainty.
The text refers to 'legal principles' and the non-binding nature of the condition.
4
Examine the procedural question
If a Hanafi judge has already decreed maintenance in dirhams, can a Shafi'i judge later decree provisions? The Hanafi answer is no, because the marriage relationship is the primary cause for maintenance, and the prior judgment stands.
This prevents contradiction between madhhabs in the same case.
5
Conclude with practical implications
The wife can seek a court order for estimated maintenance despite the condition. A prior Hanafi judgment is final and cannot be overturned by a different madhhab judge.
This lesson reinforces the importance of estimation in maintenance obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: إذا شرط عليها وقت العقد أن النفقة تموين من غير تقدير والكسوة كسوة الشتاء والصيف فهل لها بعد ذلك طلب التقدير فيهما؟ قلت: لم أره صريحاً والقواعد تقتضي أن لها ذلك لأن هذا الشرط ليس بلازم الغلة في شهر الزوج فإن كان محترفاً الخ. لأن الأداء على الدهاقين إنما يتيسر عند إدراك الغلة في كل سنة، وعلى التاجر عند اتخاذ غلة الحوانيت وغيرها في كل شهر، وعلى المحترف بالاكتساب كل يوم ا هـ قوله : (وظاهر كلامهم الخ) هذا خلاف ظاهر ما نقلناه عن الذخيرة من أن المتيسر على الدهاقين عند إدراك الغلة في كل سنة الخ. فإنه ظاهر في أنه يمهل إلى وقت إدراك الغلة في آخر السنة ثم يدفع كل سنة آخرها كما لا يخفى ولو كان المراد التعجيل لم يكن فيه تخفيف على الدهقان بل الأخف عليه كل أو كل أسبوع فتأمل قوله : (وصرح به في التجنيس في نفقة الشهر الخ) أقول : المدعي كون الخيار للزوح وما استدل به عليه من كلام التجنيس مفيد أن الخيار لها لا له، وكون الخيار لها ينافي كونه للزوج فتأمل. لكن كلام التجنيس لا ينافي ما مر لأن المراد به أنه لو اختار نفقة كل شهر بشهره لا أكثر فالخيار له حيث كان فيه تخفيف عليه، فإذا رضيت منه بأخذ كل يوم بيومه فلها ذلك لأنه أخف عليه من الشهر تأمل قوله : (فإن قلت إذا شرط عليها الخ قال في النهر : واعلم أنه لو شرط في العقد أن النفقة تموين كان الشرط غير لازم ولو حكم بموجب العقد حاكم يرى ذلك عرف ذلك من مارس كتبهم. بقي أنه لو حكم الحنفي بفرضها دراهم واستوفى ما لا بد منه هل للشافعي أن يحكم بالتموين بعد ذلك ؟ قال الشيخ قاسم في موجبات الأحكام بعد ما ذكر صورة سجل النفقة قلت: هذا دليل لما أقول من أنه ليس للشافعي ذلك بناء على أن الزوجية والقرابة سبب لوجوبها بشرطها وإن كان كل يوم سبباً لنفقته أيضاً وأن القضاء يعتمد السبب الأول وتبدل الحال والسعر ونحو ذلك يعتمد السبب الثاني ا هـ. وعلى هذا فلو حكم الشافعي بالتموين ليس للحنفي أن يحكم
If it is said: If he stipulated at the time of the contract that the maintenance is to be provisions without estimation, and the clothing is the clothing of winter and summer, then does she have the right thereafter to demand estimation in them? I say: I have not seen it explicitly, but the legal principles require that she has that right because this condition is not binding. The profit in the month of the husband: if he is a laborer, etc., because payment for farmers is only easy at the time of harvest each year, etc. He said: (And the apparent meaning of their statements, etc.) ... He said: (And he explicitly mentioned in al-Tajnis concerning the maintenance of the month, etc.) ... He said: (If it is said: If he stipulated with her, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Know that if he stipulates in the contract that the maintenance is to be provisions, the condition is not binding. And if a judge who holds that view gives a judgment according to the contract, that is known from those who have studied their books. The question remains: if a Hanafi judge decrees that it is to be estimated in dirhams and she has received what is necessary, does a Shafi'i judge have the right to then decree provisions? Shaykh Qasim said in Mujibat al-Ahkam after mentioning the form of the maintenance record: I say: This is evidence for what I say, that it is not for the Shafi'i to do that, because the marriage and kinship are the cause of its obligation with its condition, even if each day is a cause for its maintenance as well, and that the judgment relies on the first cause, while changes in situation and price and the like rely on the second cause, end quote. Based on this, if a Shafi'i judge decrees provisions, a Hanafi judge does not have the right to decree (otherwise).
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the marriage contract includes a condition that maintenance will be provided as provisions (tawmin) without a specific quantified estimate. The author asks whether the wife can later demand a formal estimation. He responds that although he has not found an explicit text, legal principles indicate she can, because such a condition is not binding (lazim). The discussion then shifts to a procedural question: if a Hanafi judge has already decreed maintenance in dirhams, can a subsequent Shafi'i judge overturn this and decree provisions? The answer is no, because the marriage relationship is the primary cause (sabab) for maintenance, and once a judgment is based on that cause, it cannot be undermined by the second cause (the passage of time or change in circumstances). Thus, the Hanafi ruling that the provision condition is not binding stands, and a Shafi'i judge cannot contradict it.

Key Terms
تموين (tawmin): Maintenance provided as provisions (food, clothing) without a specific monetary estimation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a marriage contract stipulates that maintenance will be provided as provisions (tawmin) without estimation, is this condition binding?
A) Yes, because conditions in contracts are binding
B) No, it is not binding, and the wife can demand estimation
C) Yes, but only if the husband is wealthy
D) No, but the wife forfeits her right to maintenance if she agrees

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a condition in the marriage contract to provide unspecified provisions is not binding, and the wife can demand a proper estimation.

The Obligation to Provide for the Wife's Servant: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the obligation to provide for the wife's servant and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a husband must provide for his wife's servant, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of servants, and identify the mufta bihi position adopted by later scholars.

Core Idea
The husband must provide a servant owned by the wife; later Hanafis adopted Abu Yusuf's view that more than one may be required.

In Hanafi family law, the obligation to support a wife extends to providing for her servant—but not unconditionally. The ruling depends on the husband's wealth, the servant's ownership, and the wife's needs. The Hanafi masters disagreed on how many servants must be provided. This lesson unpacks the conditions and the famous intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic obligation
The husband must provide maintenance and clothing for the wife's servant. This is wajib when the husband is wealthy. The servant must be owned by the wife (according to zahir al-riwaya) and must be exclusively dedicated to her service.
Note: The servant's maintenance is at a lower level than the wife's.
2
Locate the point of disagreement
The dispute is about the number of servants the husband must provide for. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say one servant suffices. Abu Yusuf says two or more depending on the wife's status and needs.
The disagreement is intra-madhhab, not between schools.
3
Analyse the proof of the majority
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that one servant can handle both indoor and outdoor tasks, so necessity (darura) is fulfilled by one. They rely on the principle that one person can do two jobs.
Their proof is based on sufficiency.
4
Analyse the proof of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf argues that a woman of high status may need separate servants for inside and outside especially if pregnant or of noble birth. He also narrates a different tradition allowing more based on need.
His proof is based on customary need and the wife's status.
5
Determine the thamarah and adopted view
The practical difference: under the majority view, the husband only needs to provide one servant; under Abu Yusuf's view, he may need to provide two or more. Later Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) adopted Abu Yusuf's view as the mufta bihi position.
This means in fatwa, the husband may be required to provide more than one servant if the wife's status demands it.
